Research on Characteristics of Traffic Flow Three Parameters Based on Cusp Catastrophe Theory


3
Flow theory
Jorge A. Cobb, Mohamed G. Gouda
October 1997 IEEE/ACM Transactions on Networking (TON): Volume 5 Issue 5, Oct. 1997
Publisher: IEEE Press
Bibliometrics:
Citation Count: 7
Downloads (6 Weeks): 2,   Downloads (12 Months): 14,   Downloads (Overall): 544

Full text available: PDF
Keywords: protocols, guaranteed performance protocols, protocol verification, rate reservation protocols
[result highlights]
Full Text:
Flow Theory - Networking, IEEE/ACM Transactions onIEEE/ACM TRANSACTIONS ON NETWORKING, VOL. 5, ... Cobb, Member, IEEE, and Mohamed G. GoudaAbstract—We develop a simple theory of flows to study the flowof data in real-time computing networks. Flow Theory is basedon discrete and nondeterministic mathematics, rather than thecustomary continuous ... thecustomary continuous or probabilistic mathematics. The theoryfeatures two types of flows: : smooth and uniform, and eight typesof flow operators. We prove that, if the input flow to any ofthese operators is smooth or uniform, then both ... internalbuffer and delay of that operator are bounded. Linear networksof flow operators are introduced, and their internal buffers anddelays are derived ... the internal buffers and delays of theirconstituent operators. We extend Flow Theory so that it can beused in analyzing cyclic networks and ... many rate-reservation protocols can be represented as lin-ear networks of flow operators, we use Flow Theory to prove thata number of these protocols (Stop-and-Go, Hierarchical Round-Robin, ... delays. In order to studysuch protocols, we introduce a simple theory of flows.Flow Theory is based on discrete mathematics, in whicha flow of data is represented as an infinite sequence of realnumbers. ... realnumbers. This is in contrast to fluid models of data flow, , whichneedlessly complicate the analysis. We define two propertiesof flows— —smoothness and uniformity—and introduce severalnondeterministic operators that manipulate flows. . We showthat each of these operators preserves the flow properties ofsmoothness or uniformity, while maintaining bounded delayand buffer requirements. ... form networks of arbitrary topology.We also discuss how to apply Flow Theory to the anal-ysis of rate-reservation protocols. CONCLUDING REMARKSIn this paper, we have presented a theory of flows andshowed how to use this theory in verifying rate-reservationprotocols. Flow Theory is analogous to Queueing Theory inthe sense that it provides a framework for the analysis ... analysis of delaysand buffer requirements in a network. The two theories differ,however, in that Flow Theory’s objective is to obtain upperbounds on these values in ... to obtain the average of these values ina probabilistic network.Flow Theory is both rich and effective. The richness of thistheory is ... number of concepts using relativelysimple proofs. The effectiveness of the theory is demonstratedby our ability to verify many existing rate-reservation pro-tocols ... our ability to verify many existing rate-reservation pro-tocols using the theory. . The richness and effectiveness ofthis theory ... make it a prime candidate for designing futurerate-reservation protocols.In using Flow Theory to study rate-reservation protocols,we produced a number of surprising results. ...
... a delay bound only for the first packet of a flow. . Incontrast, our analysis of the same protocol yielded a ... computer uses any of thesethree timestamp protocols.A different characterization of flows ... named is givenin [6], where is a measure of the flow burstiness, andis the flow rate. We chose not to adopt this property intoour framework ... directions are possible for future work on FlowTheory. First, the theory can be applied in designing newrate-reservation protocols, which is the ... protocols, which is the case in [4] and [9].Second, the theory can be applied to other problems in real-time networks, such ... could be developed to analyze acyclicor cyclic networks. Fourth, the theory may be enhanced byrelaxing the flow conservation property. This would allowthe modeling of broadcast capabilities and ... capabilities and the effect of datacompression/decompression algorithms applied to a flow ... as ittraverses a network.APPENDIXPROOF OF SELECTED THEOREMSRecall that the buffer flow is defined asIt follows from this definition (by induction on ... 5, NO. 5, OCTOBER 1997Proof of Theorem 2Let the input flow of the flow ... operator be , the output flowbe , and the buffer flow be .From the definition of buffer capacity, we are required ... buffer capacity, we are required toshow that for any buffer flow and anyFrom the definition of delay, we are given thatSince ... of , it followsthatProof of Theorem 6Let be the input flow, , an output flow, , and the resultingbuffer flow of operator . Properties and prediction of flow statistics from sampled packet streams
Nick Duffield, Carsten Lund, Mikkel Thorup
November 2002 IMW '02: Proceedings of the 2nd ACM SIGCOMM Workshop on Internet measurment

Many routers can generate and export statistics on flows of packets that traverse them. Increasingly, high end routers form flow statistics from only a sampled packet stream in order to manage resource consumption involved.This paper addresses three questions. Firstly: what are the downstream consequences for the measurement infrastructure? Long traffic ...

Properties and Prediction of Flow Statistics from Sampled Packet Streams Nick Duffield Carsten Lund Mikkel ... {duffield,lund,mthorup} @research.att.com Abstract--Many routers can generate and export statistics on flows ... of packets that traverse them. Increasingly, high end routers form flow statistics from only a sampled packet stream in order to ... are the downstream consequences for the measurement infrastructure? Long traffic flows will be split up if the time between sampled pack- ... up if the time between sampled pack- ets exceeds the flow timeout. Using packet header traces we show that flows generated by increasingly prevalent pcer-to-peer applica- lions are vulnerable to ... vulnerable to this effect. Secondly: can the volume of packet-sampled flow statistics be easily determined? We develop a simple model that ... a simple model that predicts both the export rate of flow packet-sampled flow statistics and the num- ber of active flows. . It uses unsampled flow statistics---those com- monly currently collected--as its data, i.e., it does ... traffic stream can be in- ferred from the packet sampled flow statistics? We show that as well as estimating total bytes ... infer more detail, specifically the number and average length of flows in the an- sampled traffic stream, even though some flows will have no packets sampled. We believe that this information ... both for under- standing source traffic, e.g. the dependence of flow lengths on appli- cation type, and also monitoring changes in ... the composition of the traffic, e.g., a flood of short flows during a DoS attack. Criteria for General Theories of Software Engineering A GTSE needs to address all of ... needs to address all of the consideration of computer science theory, , plus considerations involved in the managerial aspects of software ... comes at a price with respect to the highly formalized theories of mathematics and science. These are able to be both ... on strong universal and timeless assumptions. Examples are that the flow of electricity through a conductor, the flow of air around an airfoil, or the flow of chemicals through a reactor will be the same ten ... years from now as they are now. However, basing a theory of software engineering on such assumptions as the flow ... of adoptions for a new software engineering product or the flow of data through an evolving software product being the same ... being the same ten years from now will lead to theories with very short lifetimes. As a result, a GTSE will ... wide range of software situations, stakeholders, and products. Compared to theories in mathematics and science, where the modernist criteria of being ... people and software products makes the postmodern [1] criteria of theories ... being oral, particular, local, and timely more applicable. In developing Theory W [2], we used a set of criteria based on ... and failed software projects. Subsequently, we researched the literature for theory criteria and found good examples in [3] (importance, preciseness and ... prediction). In comparing these with our previous criteria for evaluating Theory W (simple, general, specific, accurate, analytic, predictive, diagnostic, synthetic, generative), ... criteria: 1. Utility. Particularly in a value-based context, does the theory favor addressal of critical success factors rather than trivia? 2. ... critical success factors rather than trivia? 2. Generality. Does the theory cover a wide range of situations and concerns (procedural, technical, ... and concerns (procedural, technical, economic, human)? 3. Practicality. Does the theory help address users’ practical needs with respect to prediction, diagnosis, ... generation of good practices, and explanation? 4. Preciseness. Does the theory provide situation-specific and accurate guidance? 5. Parsimony. Does the theory avoid excess complexity? Is it simple to understand, learn, and ... simple to understand, learn, and apply? 6. Falsifiability. Is the theory coherent enough to be empirically refuted? II. Having the SCSs negotiate a win-win set of ... a win-win set of product and process plans (involving decision theory) ); 4. Controlling progress toward SCS win-win realization, including adaptation ... toward SCS win-win realization, including adaptation to change (involving control theory) ). The resulting Value-Based Software Engineering (VBSE) process is summarized ... in the keynote talk, and are documented in [5]. Abstract:
<p>In the traditional maximum-flow problem, the goal is to transfer maximum flow in a network by directing, in each vertex in the ... network by directing, in each vertex in the network, incoming flow to outgoing edges. The problem corresponds to settings in which ... with no central authority. In particular, in many applications of flow networks, the vertices correspond to decision-points controlled by different and ... different companies, with different destination objectives. This suggests that the maximum-flow problem should be revisited, and examined from a game-theoretic perspective. ... from a game-theoretic perspective. We introduce and study \em multi-player flow games (MFGs, for short). Essentially, the vertices of an MFG ... players, and a player that owns a vertex directs the flow that reaches it. Each player has a different target vertex, ... and the objective of each player is to maximize the flow that reaches her target vertex. We study the stability of ... of MFGs are unbounded. That is, the reduction in the flow due to selfish behavior is unbounded. We study the problem ... good news and consider a variant of MFGs in which flow may be swallowed. For example, when routers in a communication ... incentivize selfish behavior, a Nash Equilibrium that achieves the maximum flow always exists, and can be found in polynomial time. Finally, ... in which the strategies of the players may use non-integral flows,

Network utility maximization in two-way flow scenario
Fei Ge, Liansheng Tan
April 2014 ACM SIGCOMM Computer Communication Review: Volume 44 Issue 2, April 2014
Publisher: ACM
Bibliometrics:

Downloads (6 Weeks): 2,   Downloads (12 Months): 10,   Downloads (Overall): 140

Full text available: PDF
A communication network usually has data packets and acknowledge (ACK) packets being transmitted in opposite directions. ACK packet flows may affect the performance of data packet flows, which is unfortunately not considered in the usual network utility maximization (NUM) model. This paper presents a NUM model in networks with two-way ...
Keywords: data flow and ack flow, network utility maximization

Performance analysis of LAS-based scheduling disciplines in a packet switched network
Idris A. Rai, Guillaume Urvoy-Keller, Mary K. Vernon, Ernst W. Biersack
June 2004 SIGMETRICS '04/Performance '04: Proceedings of the joint international conference on Measurement and modeling of computer systems
Publisher: ACM
Bibliometrics:
Citation Count: 31
Downloads (6 Weeks): 2,   Downloads (12 Months): 11,   Downloads (Overall): 546

Full text available: PDF
The Least Attained Service (LAS) scheduling policy, when used for scheduling packets over the bottleneck link of an Internet path, can greatly reduce the average flow time for short flows while not significantly increasing the average flow time for the long flows that share the same bottleneck. No modification of ...

This paper deals with the assessment of accuracy of simulation models from the perspective of dynamic object flows. Dynamic objects (also called temporary entities or transactions) move physically or logically from one model component to another and represent entities such as aircraft, data packet, passenger, and vehicle. (2) Missing Flow Sequence Errors: The model is said to have missing flow error if the executable model does not generate flow traces that exercise the flow patterns specified in the flow specification. This may be due to missing flows in the model implementation. That is, some object flows that are feasible in the real world domain are not ... im-plemented in the computerized model. Our technique catches all possible flow sequence er-rors in the model. Animated Flow Maps for Visualizing Human Movement: Two Demonstrations with Air Traffic and Twitter Data
Su Yeon Han, Keith C. Clarke, Ming-Hsiang Tsou
November 2017 LENS'17: Proceedings of the 1st ACM SIGSPATIAL Workshop on Analytics for Local Events and News
Publisher: ACM
Bibliometrics:
Citation Count: 0

Full text available: PDF
We present a novel flow mapping method called Animated Flow Mapper. Conventional flow mapping uses the thickness of a flow line to differentiate the volume of a flow and arrows to represent the direction. These flow mapping methods have suffered from problems of occlusion especially for visualizing large volumes of ...
Keywords: Twitter, animated map, flow map, air traffic
[result highlights]
Full Text:
occlusion of the conventional flow mapping method. Without the thick lines and arrows, the use ... map. Therefore, visualizing thin dashed lines without arrows reveals more flow lines than visualizing with various width of lines with arrows. ... width of lines with arrows. In other words, the animated flow ... maps help the users to explore more details of the flow lines by reducing overlapping lines compared to the flow maps that have various widths of line with arrows (Table ... line with arrows (Table 9). Another merit of the Animated Flow Mapper is that it works better than the static map ... the static map in terms of differentiating the direction of flows, , especially when many arrows are overlapping (Table 3 and ... The results of the case studies show that the animated flow map has advantages over the flow tree. The straighter flow lines of the Animated Flow Mapper are simpler than the arbitrary and winding flow lines of the flow tree. The common downside of the design of the flow tree is that it describes unrealistic volume of flows; ; the volume of each flow increases or decreases between an origin and a destination. However, ... decreases between an origin and a destination. However, the Animated Flow Mapper describes the constant volume of flow between an origin and a destination. Therefore, the Animated Flow Mapper describes more realistic quantities of flows than the flow trees. ACKNOWLEDGMENTS This material is based upon work supported by ... Goodchild, M. Yuan, and T. J. [email protected] ABSTRACT We present a novel flow mapping method called Animated Flow Mapper. Conventional flow mapping uses the thickness of a flow line to differentiate the volume of a flow and arrows to represent the direction. These flow mapping methods have suffered from problems of occlusion especially for ... especially for visualizing large volumes of data, and when many flows converge at--or diverge from--single points. The Animated Flow Mapper aims to circumvent these problems of occlusion and to ... provide a more effective visualization of the patterns of the flows. . The method uses thin dashed lines of equal width, ... which are animated to represent the directions and volumes of flows of moving objects by repeatedly redrawing each dashed-line at different ... human subject opinion survey show the advantages of the Animated Flow Mapper are comparable to other flow mapping methods. KEYWORDS flow map; animated map; air traffic; Twitter 1 INTRODUCTION1 Flow maps are cartographic representations of sets of linkages among pairs ... connected by lines, with the line forming the thematic symbol. Flow maps have been widely used to visualize not only the ... objects such as human migration [2], commuting [3], air traffic flows [4], goods being traded (e.g., wine exports from France [5]), ... being traded (e.g., wine exports from France [5]), and subsurface flow in a watershed [6], but also the movement of intangible ... social networks [8]. Research has identified the main challenge to flow mapping, that is, displaying a large number of connecting lines ... [9-12], especially where the lines converge. One of the traditional flow mapping methods created by Tobler [2, 13] used variable thicknesses ... used variable thicknesses of lines to differentiate the amount of flow and arrows to represent the direction of flow. . This method often creates flow maps where a few thick lines occupy considerable space and ... maps especially when the data size is big, or the flows are focused on single points, such as major cities. Some ... have reduced the visual clutter by merging and rerouting the flow lines. They have developed visualizations of flows that look like a tree – i.e., the flow has a few major branches coming from one origin, and ... cost to the viewer is that the arbitrary and winding flow lines of the tree-like flow maps are visually misleading and show incorrect information in terms ... show incorrect information in terms of the volumes of the flows (see section 4.2 for details). permissions from [email protected] LENS'17, November ...
We propose a new flow mapping method called Animated Flow Mapper. We focus not on developing an algorithm to generalize ... We focus not on developing an algorithm to generalize complex flow lines, but on the design of flow lines to improve the visual effectiveness of flow maps. The new design of flow lines was developed based on Tobler’s flow mapping method [2], and aims to decrease the visual clutter ... and improve the understanding of movement patterns by animating the flow lines. We differentiate the volume of flows by varying the movement speed (frame rate) of flow lines. To remove the need for arrows, the direction is ... arrows, the direction is represented by repeatedly shifting the dashed flow ... lines to give the appearance of animated movement in the flow direction. In the demonstrations, the Animated Flow Mapper was used to visualize air traffic flows and movements of humans using geo-tagged Twitter messages. For comparison ... testing, the same data were also visualized by two other flow mapping methods, Tobler’s Flow Mapper [13] and Flow Map Layout [11]. In addition, we conducted n opinion survey ... opinion survey to test the cognitive effectiveness of the animated flow ... maps in terms of differentiating the directions and volumes of flows. . By the comparisons and the survey, we address the ... survey, we address the usefulness and effectiveness of the Animated Flow Mapper. 2 BACKGROUND 2.1 Two styles of distributive ?low maps ... 2.1 Two styles of distributive ?low maps Various types of flow ... maps have been developed. Parks [18] identified three types: distributive flow maps, network flow maps and radial flow ... maps. Later Slocum [19] identified two more different types, continuous flow maps, and telecommunications flow ... maps. Among them, the research presented here only considers distributive flow maps which describe “the movement of commodities, people, or ideas ... ideas between geographic regions” [19]. Regarding the design of distributive flow maps, two principal styles have been developed: Tobler’s flow map and the flow tree. The first consists of straight or arc-shaped flow lines that connect origins and destinations [e.g., 2, 20-23]. The ... origins and destinations [e.g., 2, 20-23]. The other style of flow map is the flow tree [11, 12, 14-16, 24]. In this case, the flow lines are rarely straight and consist of winding or spiral ... spiral link lines. The maps that have straight or arc-shaped flow lines have methodological origins in Tobler’s flow ... maps [2]. Tobler developed a software program to automatically draw flow lines on a digital map. In 2004, this software became ... connect origins and destinations, arrows to display the directions of flows, , and various thicknesses of lines to represent the different ... various thicknesses of lines to represent the different volumes of flows – i.e., the thicker the line, the larger the flow. . The second style ... geographically similar origins and destinations. The second style of distributive flow map is the flow tree. A flow tree typically has a thick flow line (trunk), and this trunk is separated into multiple smaller ... separated into multiple smaller lines (branches). The thickness of the flow lines is proportional to the volume of flows. . One of the first flow tree maps was Charles Joseph Minard’s map of French wine ... created in 1864 [5]. Abstract:
<p>We present a novel flow mapping method called Animated Flow Mapper. Conventional flow mapping uses the thickness of a flow line to differentiate the volume of a flow and arrows to represent the direction. These flow mapping methods have suffered from problems of occlusion especially for ... especially for visualizing large volumes of data, and when many flows converge at--or diverge from--single points. The Animated Flow Mapper aims to circumvent these problems of occlusion and to ... provide a more effective visualization of the patterns of the flows. . Title:
Time-shift scheduling—fair scheduling of flows in high-speed networks

Estimating flow distributions from sampled flow statistics
Nick Duffield, Carsten Lund, Mikkel Thorup
October 2005 IEEE/ACM Transactions on Networking (TON): Volume 13 Issue 5, October 2005
Publisher: IEEE Press
Bibliometrics:
Citation Count: 40
Downloads (6 Weeks): 3,   Downloads (12 Months): 22,   Downloads (Overall): 871

Full text available: PDF
Passive traffic measurement increasingly employs sampling at the packet level. Many high-end routers form flow statistics from a sampled substream of packets. Sampling controls the consumption of resources by the measurement operations. However, knowledge of the statistics of flows in the unsampled stream remains useful, for understanding both characteristics of ...
Keywords: measurement, sampling methods, measurement errors, packet sampling, IP flows, maximum likelihood estimation
[result highlights]

CONCLUSIONS AND FURTHER WORKThis paper was concerned with deriving detailed flow statis-tics of Internet traffic from sampled flow statistics. Althoughmodification of router sampling schemes might help here, wedid ... consider these, since we wish to provide methods thatapply to flow statistics available today. The inherent difficultyof the problem is that ... washes out distribution detail.We proposed two inference methods for sampled flows thatextract smoothed information about the flow length distribution.With scaling, the hard work was in adjusting the ... toextend this approach to tune the distribution of weights fromlonger flows. . An open question is whether a similar analysisworks in ... related problem of inferringthe total bytes and duration of original flows from the corre-sponding statistics of sampled flows.ACKNOWLEDGMENTThanks are due to ...
